1)  
About the Unification Flag  
Everything in the universe was created through the relationship of giving and receiving. This flag symbolizes that the universe is structured around God, just as the solar system is formed around the sun in which humans live. The center of this flag symbolizes that all our ideals are united. Around this center, 12 lines are drawn radially, with the four thick lines indicating the four directions. For a single existence to stand firm, the four directions must be established; in other words, it is a foundation. The next 12 lines represent the years and months centered on the four directions of east, west, south, and north, and they revolve in a relationship of giving and receiving.  
<Picture: 015007.jpg>  
[The basic color of the flag is a red design on a white background.]  
Overall, it expresses the helm of a ship, indicating that we ourselves must steer this universe.  
Thus, within the flag lies everything that embodies our ideal of the principle of creation. Originally, a flag symbolizes a nation. Currently, this unification flag represents our church, but our ideal is not just the church; it symbolizes the hope of all history, the hope of modern times and the future, a world that aligns with God's heart, a world where God's purpose of creation is fulfilled, and that shining day. January 28, 1965 (Thursday), Tokyo Church, Japan.  
* This message has been translated from the Japanese collection of words titled <御言集 (Words Collection)>, Volume 1 (published on February 21, 1980).  
8   About the Unification Flag  
Therefore, those who keep this flag in their hearts and live with God's heart symbolize the power to overcome all trials and rebellious forces of Satan.  
Thus, if you believe this and move forward with courage, no matter where you go, God will work with you alongside this flag. *  

2)  
The Last of Jesus and Our Resolve  
Matthew 27:45-56  
We know that Jesus is the Savior. If Jesus is truly the Savior, then this universe must accept Jesus and his ideals, regardless of whether anyone believes or acknowledges him. Moreover, if God exists, it is only right that God fulfills the ideals of the Savior.  
The Savior is indispensable to humanity and also indispensable to God. Therefore, it is true that the Savior is essential to all existence, from the smallest to the greatest in the universe.  
Given this relationship and connection, it is natural that both God and all humanity, as well as all things, must center their lives around Jesus.  
God's heart, the heart of a parent  
Thus, Jesus' desire is the desire of the earth, the desire of heaven, the desire of humanity, and the desire of God. This desire is an absolute one that must be fulfilled at any time and in any era, transcending history, time, and the past, present, and future.  
January 31, 1965 (Sunday), Tokyo Church, Japan.  
* This message has been translated from the Japanese collection of words titled <御言集 (Words Collection)>, Volume 1 (published on February 21, 1980).  
10   The Last of Jesus and Our Resolve  
Based on this foundation of desire, Jesus was sent from heaven to this world, but has his desire been fulfilled on earth? Has heaven and humanity achieved God's desire in this universe? It is clear that this has not happened. Why? The reason is that a desire contrary to the original desire appeared on this earth before Jesus' desire could manifest. The desire that appeared on this earth did not manifest as the original desire that humanity wished for, but became a desire that opposed God or heaven.  
Therefore, the true desire must stand in a position to reject such desires. To reject that and seek to fulfill the original desire is none other than God's desire. Thus, to resolve this, God had to send a Savior to the earth.  
However, did the desire, purpose, and ideals that Jesus brought about come to fruition on this earth through a pure path? They did not. This is because the love of this earth, which is contrary to God, is a desire centered on Satan, and since it has established a foundation with a purpose centered on Satan, the greater the environment it creates, the more negatively or oppositely it manifests against Jesus' desire, purpose, and ideals. There, God, even before Jesus came to this earth, sought to create an expectation of Jesus' victory so that this opposing desire and purpose could be realized globally.  
In the ideal world of original creation, there is no need for a Savior, religion, or prayer. The need for a Savior indicates that one has fallen. If one had not fallen, expressing feelings with God and encountering God in life itself would be a religion beyond religion and a prayer beyond prayer. Living such a life itself would destroy Satan's desires on earth. This was the fight that Jesus had to engage in.  
However, our ancestors were not ancestors suitable for God's purpose of creation. In the world of God's ideal of creation through the Word, everything within the universe belonging to God's son was to globalize or idealize that lifestyle in harmony with God's heart. In other words, God wanted to rejoice with humanity and sing happiness with humanity while standing in the position of a true parent in our lives. This was God's purpose in creating humans as the highest beings. We know this fact through the principles.  
Fallen Adam and Eve gave birth to Cain and Abel, and the Adam family began. However, that family was not the family that God desired. Although many descendants were born from that lineage, those descendants felt even greater sorrow. We must recognize that the more numerous they became, the more they increased the conditions of sorrow for God.  
When we consider that they formed one nation, one state, and one world of humanity, God himself could not just leave it as it was. From the original heart standard of the True Parents, although they had fallen, humanity, who were beloved children, could not be left to Satan, and seeing them in a state of sorrow, God could not abandon them. From a heavenly perspective, it could not be done either. Therefore, no matter what path of suffering he had to walk, God's heart was to save all of humanity. Thus, the more humanity increased, the more they spread on earth, the more God's heart felt an unbearable pain and misery.  
In response, Satan accuses God, saying,  
"Originally, your ideal was to embrace the world and humanity centered on Adam and build a world of eternal love, but now a world centered on me has been created. Are there any true children you desire in this world? Is there a family? Or a nation?"  
When Satan accuses God from such a position, God has no choice but to acknowledge such accusations.  
Because there is a heart standard of a parent-child relationship between God and humanity, one cannot avoid such a position. From here, the history of restoration until now has been to overcome this enemy and return this world to the ideal world of creation that God desires.  
Until now, God has sought to send a Savior through the providential course. The hope of that Savior spans the entire world and the universe. In that hope, the time when that desire is fulfilled, that is, when Jesus came, God had to find one person who would contribute absolutely to God in order to create a foundation that could block Satan's opposition against the Savior. Thus, from the Adam family through the Noah family to Abraham, at last, one person was found. We know that it took 2,000 years of history to find one person who would obey God and be taken from the world of Satan. By establishing a standard of absolutely believing in God and not betraying God no matter what painful things happened, we understand that God's providence became centered around one human being on earth.  
God's Hope  
Abraham is the ancestor of faith. God sought to teach Abraham, the ancestor of faith, the path that He originally hoped for before Adam's fall, guiding him so that he would not be subjected to the temptations of the world of Satan in his inner and outer life.  
God took Abraham, the son of Terah, who was an idol merchant, and moved him from his living environment to another place, putting him through bitter hardships and harsh trials. However, even amidst such trials, we must recognize that God led Abraham to keep the thought of the promise to God and the thought of contributing to God as absolute standards, waiting for such a day.  
God commanded Abraham to leave his homeland, Ur of the Chaldeans. Until then, Abraham had historical, emotional, and circumstantial environments, as well as a desire-centered environment. He must have had an environment centered on his parents, siblings, and relatives. God called him from such a situation. Despite having such a homeland, Abraham responded to God's call and left that place. He started from there.  
The land that Abraham aimed for was not a place he admired. It was a foreign land he did not know at all. God knew that many difficulties awaited him there, and Abraham himself knew it too. However, he courageously left his homeland, Ur of the Chaldeans, in obedience to God's command.  
This serves as a significant trial (lesson) for us who are engaged in a life of faith.  
Abraham lived as a wanderer in a foreign land, believing in God's command, but if he did not truly love and believe in God, there would have been many times he could have betrayed God.  
However, Abraham, who consistently admired God until the end, became the son whom God could trust, and for the first time since humanity's fall, he decisively established one person who was in accordance with God's will on this earth.  
And then there is the offering of Isaac. Abraham's heart, as he prepared to offer Isaac as a sacrificial offering on the altar of Mount Moriah, was that no matter what happened, the God who promised him would surely fulfill that promise. It was because Abraham believed this that he had the strength to overcome any trials or persecutions from Satan, allowing him to complete the offering of Isaac safely. Thus, we know that by discerning Satan, God created an expectation to relate only to one person, Abraham.  
God's hope centered around one person, Abraham, was a family that could believe in God more than that one person. If such a family were to be formed, God desired a clan, and if a nation were to be formed, He desired a state. Furthermore, when a nation was established, He wished to establish one world through that nation. In this way, from the small to the great, from one person to the whole, God has been trying to elevate it to the ideal world of creation He wishes to achieve.  
From there, God directly led one person, Abraham, to a designated area, creating an expectation of victory in the family by the time of Jacob.  
Jacob also left his father's homeland and went to Haran. Because of this, Jacob had to abandon his attachment to his homeland, such as his affections, circumstances, and future hopes, leaving behind all his living environment. With nothing but his body, he headed to Haran, and his heart was solely devoted to admiring God.  
If Jacob had any hope, it was the assurance that God would bless him, and the certainty that God would be with him wherever he was. Jacob considered this the highest glory and the utmost authority.  
The path of restoration for the fallen Rachel  
Thus, even the painful path in the land of Haran was not distressing for him. The deeper he fell into the depths of suffering, the less he could open his heart to God. While tending to the sheep and listening to their bleating, he always prayed,  
"Just as I love this flock of sheep, please love these descendants of Jacob, who are blessed."  
When he saw all things, he prayed,  
"God! Just as I love each and every one of these things as symbols of the Israelite nation, please love our many descendants."  
Jacob's 21 years of life was a life of relying on God for everything and entrusting everything to God. By striving to approach the depths of God's heart, he expressed that his entire life must be with God and for God's glory.  
Wherever Jacob went, it was all a path of opposition, and all were imperfect environments that were not permitted, but the more difficult the environment became, the stronger Jacob's heart toward God grew. Consequently, God's heart also grew stronger.  
The more Jacob had to endure suffering or bitterness in his environment, the more God responded by opening up Jacob's path. This is a fact. We must consider that Jacob was able to safely endure the 21 years of hardship through his experiences.  
However, when the time came, Jacob realized that he had to return to his homeland, Canaan, and there were matters with his uncle Laban. Laban was the one who deceived Jacob ten times during his 21 years of living, taking away the grace of Jacob's blessings. In other words, he was a...
He was a master of multiplication, but from the perspective of providence, he was in the position of Satan who used the substance. 

In such an environment, if there is someone who truly longs for Jacob, who is genuinely loyal to God, even if he is on the side of Satan, he cannot be forgiven until Jacob's period of atonement is over. However, once that period is over or the conditions are met, God can forgive the person on Satan's side. Rachel was in such a position. She was the daughter of Laban and the wife of Jacob. She came to know over a long period that her father Laban was doing something that he should not do to Jacob. 

If Jacob were to return to Canaan, Rachel had to follow him. She knew that if someone had deceived and taken away the property that was received as a blessing from God, that person would soon receive God's punishment. When her husband Jacob was to return to his hometown, she understood that her father Laban would not give Jacob the promised property, and finally resolved to steal something of greater value than what Laban had promised Jacob. Having such a wife was an absolute condition that Jacob could not do without in fulfilling his heavenly mission. Jacob, having resolved to take back 100% of the property promised by Laban as a result of 21 years of hard work, stood in a position that said that without such conditions being established, he could not initiate familial providence according to God's providence, that is, the providence of restoration. From there, Jacob had to pack all that he could receive according to what he had promised with Laban and set out towards his hometown within three days. This was not just a matter of a single historical fact. 

For a family centered around Jacob, who had received blessings from Isaac, to enter the world of Satan as Abraham's representative and take away the beloved Rachel and property means that humans must engage in a familial struggle to discern everything from the world of Satan and transfer it to God's side. This was an absolute condition in providence. 

However, when Laban noticed that Jacob was taking his wife and property and pursued him, Rachel cleverly hid the idols that her father Laban loved and sought under the saddle so that they would not be discovered, sending Laban back to his hometown. 

The fact that Rachel, who walked the path of restoration for the fallen world of Satan, sent Laban back from the position of substance created the condition to discern the substantial Satan. In this way, the conditions pursued by Satan on earth were cut off, and the Jacob family headed towards the land of Canaan. 

Victory on Earth
Israel

Thus, even though Rachel sent her father back, Jacob still had the position that he must subdue Satan in spiritual terms. Therefore, Jacob spent the night praying by the Jabbok River, with Canaan in sight, when an angel appeared and wrestled with him for his life. To receive a blessing, Jacob could not help but fight and win, even if his opponent was an angel. With that determination, he fought through the night and won the wrestling match. Consequently, the angel dislocated Jacob's hip joint, and Jacob received a blessing from him. This left a historical account of such content. 

This history is not known to us. However, the content stands between the absolute conditions that God desires and the fact that Satan does not allow Jacob's family to belong to God's side. Yet, the Jacob family stood on the basis of victory desired by God while simultaneously cutting off the side of Satan, thus for the first time receiving the name Israel, that is, victory on this earth centered around a family. 

In Abraham's family, he became the ancestor of faith, but in Jacob, he achieved victory. From this, the nation of Israel began. 

Jacob, fearing to meet his brother Esau, set his sheep and servants in front of him. However, when he visited his hometown, why did Esau not rebel against Jacob? The act of Jacob taking away his blessing was unforgivable. Esau, who was greatly enraged, surely had thoughts of killing Jacob on the spot if he came. 

But why was he able to welcome Jacob? The underlying reason was that Jacob had repelled Rachel's father through all sorts of adventures and subdued the angel, thus establishing an internal condition that opposed the substantial Laban, who was against the so-called spiritual angel. If Esau opposed Jacob's family, which followed God's word, then God could not forgive him either. God had to protect the standard of Jacob's victory. Although Esau did not know the content that if he struck that condition, he would be in the right position, he understood that he did not want to think about it but could not help but follow it. This must be understood to have happened due to Jacob's victory and Rachel's victory. 

In this way, God established the standard of familial victory and created the nation of Israel centered around the twelve children from that family. 

Although there was much effort in sanctifying Jacob's family, from God's position, it was necessary to form a clan and a nation centered on this family, and there had to be earthly humans who could decide whether to be on God's side or Satan's side based on the conditions of atonement. This was a standard of heart or faith centered on individuals, families, nations, and states in God's providence up to that point. Or, based on the standard of keeping God's commands, that is, when Adam fell, he did not have a heart to believe in God without going through God's heart and could not keep God's commands. Although the times have passed, according to that long-standing providence of God, those who took responsibility must always center on faith, believe in God, keep God's commands, and act. Without establishing a standard that passed through God's heart, God's providence could not develop. 

From there, to lead this family, which stood on the basis of victory centered around Jacob, to Canaan, Joseph was sent in advance. God sent him on the path of suffering and placed him in trials. However, he had to believe in God, love God, walk and act with God, and not fall into any temptations of the world of Satan, maintaining a consistent heart and faith. Because Joseph lived like that in the land of Egypt, he was recognized by God as a victor. Joseph rejected the temptations of Potiphar's wife, the captain of the guard in Egypt, and even if he lost his position, he stood on the side of justice, running with a heart that loved the nation of Israel and, of course, loved God. Thus, a standard of victory for one person could be established within the realm of Egypt and in the world of Satan. God centered on that expectation gave blessings. 

Thus, Joseph became the prime minister in that land and led his family into Egypt. However, God's true desire was not just for him to become the prime minister. During that time, God intended for Joseph to have the sense of responsibility to make the Egyptian people a nation that would never oppose God's providence, but Joseph did not know that. While he could save his family, who were starving due to famine, he could not think of resolving the spiritual famine in God's providence itself. 

The Faith and Qualifications of Moses as a Leader

Although Joseph led his family, the nation went through a path of suffering over 400 years, which was also due to Joseph not fulfilling his responsibilities. If he had created an environment for the victory of his clan and, based on that, created an environment where the nation of Israel could put the Egyptian nation in the position of Cain and obey Jacob, who was in the position of Abel, then God's will would have been to create the national standard of victory for Israel from there. However, because Joseph did not know that content and could not establish that standard, God called Moses after four generations and made him take responsibility to fulfill God's wishes by sending him under Pharaoh. 

Just as God loved the nation of Israel, Moses also loved the nation of Israel. Seeing his fellow Israelites suffering and enduring in pain, Moses gave up the glory of the palace and established a heart of affection that God could love as a standard for the nation. A truly blessed nation should not have been established on such miserable results. Therefore, Moses had the conviction that God would surely lead this nation to a new hopeful land and began to contribute to God, and the faith of those who prayed to God began to pass through Moses's heart. 

The greater the external persecution, the stronger the affection for the land of Canaan, the homeland of the nation of Israel, grew in proportion to the suffering that pressed upon them. With such a heart, Moses made a vow to God, and seeing the Egyptians beating the Israelites with whips, he felt a deep need to lead the blessed nation of Israel and struck the Egyptian with a stone, killing him. From a common flat perspective, this is an unforgivable sin. However, anyone in that position would naturally act that way. When God's heart stood in such a position, God recognized that Moses's actions were on His behalf. 

The next day, seeing the Israelites quarreling, Moses tried to stop them. However, due to the person on the other side, the rumors of what had happened the previous day spread, and Moses realized that his position was in danger and fled to the Midian wilderness. 

Moses's life as a shepherd for 40 years in that place was miserable and filled with suffering, but even in that, his heart loved the nation of Israel and God more than anyone else, and he admired and loved the land of Canaan more than anyone else, which was Moses's great point. That heart was sufficient to qualify him as a leader of the nation of Israel. 

Moses's love for the land of Canaan was in line with God's hope to return the people there, so God made Moses oppose Pharaoh's palace. At that time, his wife Zipporah resolved that no matter what difficult land Moses went to, she would always be one body, becoming his hands and feet, comforting him, and sharing the responsibility of God along with Moses's difficult position. Therefore, from God's perspective, she was an absolute being indispensable for Moses to fulfill the precious providence and also became a standard of atonement. 

Moses fought many battles with Pharaoh while bringing his family along. However, even through ten miracles, Pharaoh did not want to free the nation of Israel. If Moses had only lived in Pharaoh's palace, it would have been impossible for him to fight to the end when God gave such a command. However, through the hardships of his past 40 years in the Midian wilderness, he had the firm conviction that God is always on my side, and if I stand on God's side and have a heart that is appropriate to His heart, God will protect me. 

For that reason, even when Pharaoh deceived him several times and did not send the nation of Israel back, Moses never became discouraged and fought boldly. Thus, he took advantage of the three days and brought the entire nation of Israel out from the world of Satan. 

The Heart of a Leader

This is a part of the history of the faith life of the descendants of Israel from the perspective of providence. However, from God's perspective, who leads this faith life and commands it, there was a bitter underlying reason that no one knew, which was that God had to place His beloved individuals, families, and nations in such a painful position in the relationship between God and Satan. 

What we living today must understand is that we should not be ignorant of God's internal affairs, which are moving history and commanding to fulfill the purpose of providence behind the scenes, rather than the facts that appear on history. 

The nation of Israel, which did not understand Moses's heart, did not know the heart of Moses, who was united with God, longing for Canaan, and the heart of Moses, who had to fight and win until the end. They only set out with the thought that they could return to their homeland. Because their only purpose was to return home, when faced with greater suffering and bitterness, they stood in a position of rebellion against Moses and disbelief against God. 

The internal worries of God and Moses, leading a crowd of over 600,000, were indescribable. At that time, the nation of Israel, which had to return to the land of Canaan, had to become one body, or be united internally and externally, entrusting everything to God's will, and advance as one with Moses. For example, even if half of the nation of Israel supported Satan, God had to take at least the other half of the people into the land of Canaan. Even if one-fifth or one-tenth of the nation had to be sacrificed, they had to be united with Moses to have a purpose that was in accordance with God's will and return to the land of Canaan. Only then could God's providence centered on the nation be fulfilled. 

However, at that time, the nation of Israel did not know such things. The nation of Israel, which thought only about their living conditions, had no room to think about the nation or God. They should have known what their leader's heart was like, but no one knew that. Only the nation of Israel, which looked forward to returning home and stability in life, began to complain when they faced conditions worse than those in Egypt. 

The problem started from there. If the nation of Israel were to abandon their future homeland, Canaan, and return to Egypt, no matter how much they were the nation of Israel under Moses's leadership, they would become a position completely unrelated to Moses and would also be in a position completely unrelated to God. Such a thing should not have happened to Moses or God. 

At that time, looking at such movements of the nation, Moses, as a leader, felt the bitterness of hearing complaints like, "There is no food, no water, no clothes, no place to live." The pain of being a leader was the same as God's pain in commanding. Moreover, God, seeing Moses struggling and suffering, could not help but feel double the pain. He could not help but feel pain over the betrayal of the nation of Israel, and He felt pity and sorrow for Moses. 

Among the nation of Israel, who were in such a state of disbelief, if someone had said, "O God! Punish this nation," would not God have been in a position where He truly wanted to punish them? 

However, every time that happened, Moses said, "Aren't you the chosen people of Israel whom You led out from the land of Egypt through great suffering? Wasn't the curse of many nations upon Abel a good condition for Satan?" and he acted for the sake of God's heart. Moses's such heart was what could later liberate the leaders or patriarchs of Israel and many people.
The heart of Moses, who looked upon a nation that betrayed God, would have found it easier to die himself. However, Moses thought of the historical Israelite nation that God had blessed from his ancestors until now. And when he considered God as the historical, temporal, and future God, who would be eternally with his descendants and his clans, Moses could not run away. Yet, he could neither leave them as they were nor abandon them. The anguish of Moses, who stood in such a position as a leader, was unimaginable to anyone. Thus, Moses ascended Mount Sinai and prayed for 40 days. This was because he could not enter the land of Canaan unless he became one with the nation. 

The land of Canaan was to be a place of the altar designed by God, and it had to be offered as a single sacrifice, distinguishing it from the fallen world. The land of Canaan had to be offered to God as a national sacrifice. However, the Israelite nation fell into corruption before God and before Moses. Ultimately, even Moses, who had the mission as a leader, died in the wilderness without entering the land of Canaan. The historical journey that had brought Moses to lead had thus come to an end. Here, we must understand not only the history that has appeared but also the miserable heart of God within it, and the heart of the leader who bore responsibility centered on that heart of God.

The Israelite nation, which was suffering under enemies and crossing the threshold of death with Moses, had to have a heart full of gratitude while thinking of Moses, who fought on their behalf, and God, who encouraged him and commanded him. Nevertheless, the nation clashed with one another and declared to Moses and God, "We have no God, we have no leader," while making idols, dancing, and causing chaos. The history of 2,400 years ended in such a conclusion in that desolate wilderness; what greater tragedy could there be? Yet, no one knew such a fact.

God's providence to align with the Messiah
Meanwhile, if the nation that entered the land of Canaan centered around Joshua had become one with their leader, offered the sacrifice of victory, and not divided, that Israelite nation would have become a nation that could not be protected by God. And the Israelite nation would have stood as a victorious people that Satan could not invade. However, even after entering the land of Canaan, they quarreled with one another and rebelled against the prophets or leaders sent by God, causing harm and massacres. They had continuously acted in such a manner throughout history.

God, who looked upon such actions, saw that the fulfillment of the restoration providence, in other words, the realization of the ideal nation that God desired, extended as history repeated itself, and as time flowed on, the longing for that nation grew stronger. Therefore, the more sad events occurred in history, the more tears filled God's eyes, and God's heart could not help but wander through a painful valley. No one until now has known that God, who has traversed such a miserable history, has taken on the providence of salvation.

However, God, who must achieve His purpose at all costs, looked forward to the time when that purpose would be fulfilled and sent one person who could represent the nation and the world to a single place and environment to determine the final victory and resolve the grievances of history up to that point.

Thus, with that goal in mind, God taught through numerous prophets in Israel's history that the Savior Messiah would come. He gathered the scattered nations to unify around a single temple and punished those who opposed it. If one betrayed individually, they were punished individually; if they betrayed as a family, they were punished as a family; if they betrayed as a clan, they were punished as a clan. If the nation betrayed, the nation was punished.

Through such painful experiences in history, God hoped for the day of unity, but until Jesus came, the Israelite nation did not fulfill God's hope and did not repent. They were punished and perished. They repeatedly fell into corruption when blessed and fell into corruption again when blessed. The human beings that God decided to send to fulfill His purpose in a specific time and environment had to achieve global victory based on serving His will. Yet, the nation, its leaders, and the rituals of the temple were all in positions that did not align with God's will.

The restoration providence is about establishing conditions for indemnity centered on time, so after 4,000 years, all conditions for indemnity had to be established, and a standard for national victory had to be created. From a providential perspective, it was necessary to establish a national temple, become one with that nation, and offer all national sovereignty, temples, and everything to the Messiah. God led the Israelite nation with the hope of that day, but the Israelite nation did not do so.

The attitude of the Israelite nation was that they did not care about the Son of God, the commands of leaders or prophets, or the ideals of the temple. Even after entering the land of Canaan, the Israelite nation was just concerned with their individual hopes, thinking, "As long as I can live this way, I do not need the Canaan that is the hope of the Israelite nation. I just need my worldly desires to be fulfilled." This was the same attitude they had when they came out of Egypt into the wilderness. However, God wanted the opposite of what the nation entering the land of Canaan desired. For over 2,000 years, God loved His people and traversed such a painful path.

Why was that? Because that path was meant to subdue the global Satan for the nation of hope and purpose. God wanted the Israelite nation in the land of Canaan to do that, but they did not. In the midst of this, God sought someone who was truly worthy of His hope, someone who would take responsibility by obeying His word, and someone who, like God Himself loved the future world, was concerned about the fate of the nation in a miserable position, asking if there was anyone who longed for the future Israel, the hopeful Israel. But there was none.

God's hope, Jesus' hope, the hope of history
The Israelite nation that appeared in history became a vassal of many nations and ultimately became a vassal of Rome, falling into a state of helplessness. In such a time and environment, Jesus was sent. Although the environment in the land of Israel was not prepared to believe in God, the time had come, and the promised time had arrived; that is, because the time and person were prepared on God's side, Jesus was sent at that point. Before sending Jesus into such an environment, God had to send someone who could prepare the environment to long for Jesus through history. That person with such a mission was John the Baptist.

However, from God's perspective, the very act of sending John the Baptist was God's sorrow. If the nation had become one and prepared with a heart longing for the Messiah before John was sent, there would have been no need to send John at all. However, because the nation could not unite, God had to send John to gather the Israelite nation, which had betrayed before God, centered around the land of Canaan, and connect them to Jesus. Yet, even John, swept away by the environment, could not receive Jesus, not knowing such content and God's heart. As a result, even John became a betrayer.

And because the central figure fell, the Israelite nation that should have been connected to him naturally could not help but lean toward Satan. The Israelite nation had to connect their internal ideological center of Judaism and the external Israelite state into one, and they had to welcome the Messiah as the Lord of hope. However, the Israelite people, who should have revered Jesus, sent as the Savior of Israel from God, did not know such a fact at all.

The time had come, and the prepared figure was sent from God, but there was no environment to receive the time and person. There was no foundation for God's ideal to be conveyed. The Jesus who came with the highest purpose to that unprepared environment hoped that the Israelite nation would long for the Messiah. Jesus and the Israelite nation had to become one. The nation had to follow wherever the Messiah went. The wishes of the Messiah had to become the wishes of the nation. The life of the Messiah had to become the life of the nation. The actions of the Messiah had to become the actions of the nation. They could not be divided. Yet, ultimately, the Messiah and the nation, who had to become one, were separated.

Thus, all the historical narratives that had flowed until that time, centered on the nation, and the Messiah sent to the nation stood in a position that had no historical or dimensional relationship with the Israelite nation, and Jesus had no choice but to walk the path of the cross. Through the cross, Jesus walked the final path.

After that, with the coming of the Holy Spirit and the path of resurrection, if it is said that people have relied on the spiritual Savior until now, what was God's hope for the earth? God's hope was with the Israelite nation. God's hope centered on Israel was a nation through the people. The issue was to establish a blessed nation through the blessed Israelite nation.

Jesus came to this earth to fulfill God's hope for the earth. Therefore, Jesus' hope was the same as God's hope, which was to lead the nation and move the country. It was not just a nation; it was a nation that Jesus and the Israelite nation had to achieve together. 

However, the nation that Jesus hoped for was not a nation just for that era. It was an eternal historical nation. It was a nation that would lead His people forever. Within that nation were the people, clans, families, and individuals. God's hope, the hope of Christ sent by God's will, and the historical hope of the Israelite nation that revered God were ultimately not about the nation. It was not about Jesus Himself. It was the nation that God desired, that is, God's nation. Therefore, the hope and goal of Jesus, who came to this earth as the Messiah, was the nation of Israel.

The heart of Jesus and His sorrow
Three elements are necessary to form a nation. First, there must be territory. There must be a people. And there must be sovereignty. Then, what kind of people are the people of that nation? They are the Israelite people, who have nurtured their traditions throughout history, and the territory is the blessed land of Canaan. And the central figure who establishes sovereignty must stand as a national and overall leader; the one sent for that purpose was the Messiah.

The Messiah does not become the spiritual Savior of all people by dying. He was sent as the omnipotent prince on earth and as the center of the Israelite nation and Rome. 

When Abraham was blessed, he was called from his homeland and sent unconditionally. Jacob was blessed and left his homeland to enter a land where enemies were present. Moses was also sent after receiving a promise of blessing into the wilderness. 

In the same way, it was necessary to build the Israelite nation centered on Jesus, to determine the absolute land of Canaan, to determine the absolute Israelite people, and to establish the absolute sovereignty of Israel. And the greatest person had to be raised to create a new ideology of the nation centered on Jesus, a new culture, and a national tradition, and to surpass the global center of Rome, which was moving the entire world of that era. This was Jesus' responsibility.

However, when did Jesus ever reveal His dignity as the Son of God in God's kingdom? Did He ever command people as the King of all people to listen to His commands? Was there anyone on earth who truly welcomed the Messiah, who was born as the only begotten Son of the Heavenly Father, saying, "Indeed, you are the prince of heaven"? There was no such individual, nor was there a family. There was no clan, nor was there a nation. Without a nation, there could be no reason for a state to exist.

Thus, Jesus could not convey even a complete teaching about an individual during His time on earth. How could Jesus, who could not speak of a complete teaching to individuals, speak about families? How could He, who could not speak about families, convey His teachings about the nation, state, or world? Therefore, no one knew the inner heart of Jesus.

At that time, there may have been many who followed Jesus for His numerous miracles or to obtain bread. Thousands and thousands of people gathered to satisfy their desires, but there was no one who resolved to become an indispensable person to Jesus, saying, "I will be someone who truly knows your heart." Since there was no such person, there could be no such family. Since there was no such family, of course, there could be no nation. Therefore, we must understand that Jesus lived a miserable and pitiful life, inexpressibly painful.

Wasn't this evident in His prayer in Gethsemane? The three disciples shared three years of joy and sorrow with Jesus and swore, "Wherever you go, I will follow you," yet they fell asleep during each of the three prayer times in Gethsemane.

This was the final outcome of the disciples who had admired Jesus. Jesus prayed, deciding whether to die or to choose life, saying, "If it is possible, let this cup pass from me; yet not as I will, but as you will." He repeated such a prayer three times.

Even at that critical moment of deciding whether to die on the cross, the disciples, who could not become one with Jesus, could not stand in a position to die in His place. A person who cannot keep a promise at the time of making a promise cannot stand in the position of a leader who fulfills that promise. Thus, when Jesus was arrested, they all fled. This was the response of people to God's 4,000 years of history.

God sent numerous prophets and ancestors, promising that if the nation betrayed Him, He would punish them, correct their wrong paths, and renew His promises. Two thousand years ago, He sent Jesus, the hope of all people, to the Israelite nation. However, the Israelite nation betrayed the Messiah, who was to guide their fate and oversee the fate of the world. There has been no more tragic event since the beginning of history.

The fall of the human ancestors occurred in a position where there was no labor from their ancestors, but the Israelite nation, through 4,000 years of history, treated the Messiah in such a way when they were in a position to receive Him, which was a complete betrayal of the ancestors who had labored for thousands of years and a complete betrayal of God's labor over thousands of years. This resulted in the conclusion that there was no greater sin against God's ideals, the purpose of Jesus' life, and the purpose of all humanity. For that reason, the history of the Israelite nation could not help but become miserable thereafter.
The nation that persecuted and abused the Israelite people has perished. Under God's protection, the nation that had been nurtured has become a pitiful people, wandering for 2,000 years after the death of Jesus, unable to assert any national identity centered around a leader. Ultimately, the result of the Holocaust, which brought about the slaughter of six million during World War II by Hitler, was a natural retribution. This was because they had to pay historically for their national sins. By that time, they had lost the 4,000 years of history that had been built up until the death of Jesus. From there, a new history began. Through this miserable history, the Israelite nation, built upon 4,000 years of God's labor, faced total destruction.

After the resurrection of Jesus, Christians became the Second Israel centered around Jesus, promising a global beginning based on national standards. The ideal that the Messiah had envisioned progressed into a spiritual standard. This is the history of the development of Christianity up to now. 

Christianity bears the responsibility to settle the historical sins committed by the Israelite people, and it must transcend death. For an individual to be saved, they must go through the ordeal of atonement, akin to death. For a family to be saved, families must go through the ordeal of atonement, akin to death. For a nation to be saved, nations must go through such an ordeal of atonement, akin to death. 

On the path of martyrdom, shedding blood while appealing to God's lament, Christians must cry out to God, saying, "Please send us the promised Lord of the Second Advent. The Israelite people doubted the first Messiah until the end, but we have become a nation of faith that longs for and welcomes the Lord of the Second Advent, so please send Him to us." Thus, they must transcend the path of atonement through death, beyond the grave, raising their hands to God in supplication, which is the fate of Christianity.

Now, after 2,000 years of history, the ideals of Christianity stand on altars of countless blood and sacrifices, capable of moving half of the world. The current democratic world is centered around Christian culture. Furthermore, God's providence has expanded from the individual providence era to the family providence era, the clan providence era, the national providence era, and now to the state providence era. God has been expanding the stage of providence to create a world that is worthy of His ideal of creation. That ideal world is not two; it is absolutely one. However, in the present age, Christians in the position of the Second Israel are fighting among denominations. If they forget how much effort God has made to leave them in history or what their responsibilities are, then Christians will stand in the same position as the Israelite people did in opposition to God in the past.

The fortunes of external nations across the world are heading in one direction. As the center of that external world and the spiritual guidance, Christianity holds the position that it had the privilege to take responsibility for the national spirit of the Israelite nation during the time of Jesus, allowing for internal and external unification at the time of the Messiah's coming.

Now, the world has become one stage where it can freely move anywhere. The United States corresponds to the ancient Rome. The democracy that follows them has a historical tradition centered on Christianity. 

So what kind of movement must Christianity engage in today? Just as the time of Jesus was a difficult period with continuous conflicts among denominations, factions, and nations, such a period will undoubtedly manifest in this democratic age. Therefore, just as the current democracy cannot lead the world, the Roman principle could not lead the world either. The ideal led by the Messiah was higher than that led by Rome.

In today’s democratic world, such a situation cannot be avoided. If Christianity, which must maintain and solidify its internal position, fights among itself, it will bring about miserable results in this end time. Thus, numerous denominations must initiate a global unification movement from within. 

The state of Korea, where our principle has emerged, stands in a position similar to that of the Israelite people in the past. In such a world, our Unification Church must historically undergo a humiliating path corresponding to the time of Jesus to create the expectation of unification, as its name suggests. 

Thus, we have faced numerous oppressions from various sovereignties and walked the path of many persecutions, creating the so-called expectation of victory in an environment where various things are not permitted. Communism is now emerging in response to democracy. It stands on a systematic ideal based on empirical science, confronting democracy. Someone is needed to overcome this. A truly empirical and practical ideological system centered on God, one that can be experienced in life processes and can create an ideal world where God’s existence is acknowledged, must emerge; otherwise, we cannot overthrow communism.

If this does not emerge and Cain and Abel continue to fight until the end, they will perish together, and if both are destroyed, there will be no salvation. Cain killed Abel in the Adam family. Cain rebelled against God. Therefore, God gave birth to Seth. Throughout history, Cain has always struck first against God. The losing side has always struck first. Thus, looking at the situation of these last days, the principles of worldism, ideology, and spiritualism centered on God will emerge. That principle will surpass all existing ideological systems and align with practical and empirical life, thus becoming the center and substitute for the overall values. The substituted principle does not merely acknowledge God’s existence ideologically but recognizes God as the center of life, creating a system of ideals, ideologies, or religious systems that can establish a foundation for such faith.

The God we think of ideologically is far from us. The God we have known from before is distant. The God we worship through faith is far from us. We need a God of life. Humans yearn for joy that can respond to their circumstances and emotions. That is where the problem lies. No matter how high one's global status or honor may be, if it does not have value that responds to one’s emotional state or circumstances, it is meaningless. If that value is recognized as irreplaceable by anyone in the world or by all people in the current two major camps, that person can become a master who can move even God beyond history.

Humans have emotions. Humans must live. To live, they must cooperate. The purpose must be through desire. Furthermore, in life, one must have a value system that aligns with their purpose, an individual value system, a family value system, and a common value system shared among families, which is the absolute value. This is the so-called value that aligns with God's purpose. It is not a matter of a distant world. If one recognizes it as a value beyond life value, then there is no greater desire as a human, and there is no greater success for us. God wants to be acknowledged as an infinitely valuable being among the many conditions of hopeful human life and as a being who is praised and revered.

Therefore, what the people of the world first seek is not a simple ideal or any principle, but the circumstances of life. The emotion that exists there is the emotion of the Messiah, and the reason that emotion is needed is that it becomes the source that can achieve any purpose.

That circumstance is one that can establish relationships on the stage of life. Even if heaven and earth are divided, it is a circumstance that can unite, even if people are divided. That desire can be said to be a common purpose for anyone. Can’t we say to the person next to us, "That desire is my desire," and celebrate and give thanks for that success? In this modern world, it is not an emotion or desire for individuals to envy each other's success.

Look at the existence of God, who is thorough in this value system, and look at God's heart. Look at God's circumstances. Look at God's desires. Everything must align with God's purpose, with God as the subject, and we must stand in the objective position to become one. When that happens, if God rejoices, we rejoice together. My joy becomes God's joy itself, and my sorrow becomes God's sorrow itself. Only then can we discover ourselves as the foundation of the expectation of a valuable existence that sees God's reality in life. That value is one that cannot be exchanged for anything in the universe. That is why Jesus said, "What will it profit a man if he gains the whole world and loses his own soul?" (Matthew 16:26). That is the truth.

One's value is greater than the value of the universe, and living in that context, one feels that there is no greater happiness than this; that is the life of the Messiah. If that is inherited through individuals, families, clans, and nations to the world, that is the world that Jesus desired. If that happens, it will become the kingdom that God Himself wanted to establish as the ideal of creation. The life itself included in that is one that exists with God's value. God desired that.

Considering all this, what should the individuals gathered here hope for? The desires we have had until now are not the desires we originally wanted. The homes we live in are not the homes we originally wanted. Our society, our nation, and our world are not what we desired. Everything is centered around the concept of life, family, society, and nation based on oneself. Although the time has not yet come, when it does, these concepts will easily betray God. That is why Jesus said, "If anyone comes to me and does not hate his own father and mother and wife and children and brothers and sisters, yes, and even his own life, he cannot be my disciple. And whoever does not bear his own cross and come after me cannot be my disciple." (Luke 14:26-27).

What should we, who are in such a position in the present age, do? Before God Himself judges, we must judge ourselves. To be a person who has the authority to judge before the judgment of the world, one must be a being who has passed the judgment of a nation. In other words, one must have the authority and qualification of judgment above the national standard. Therefore, we, who are learning how the historical background of emotions has moved according to the principle, must establish that position through all internal affairs, mind and body, and practice.

The current world is divided into two major ideologies: communism or democracy. However, God is neither communism nor democracy. It is unificationism. What can individuals do standing just before such things are realized? God tells us to judge ourselves before judging our families. When we do that, God shows compassion.

So what is judgment? It is to completely subjugate. Even if one is alive, it is better to act as if dead. The purpose lies there. That is, no matter what happens, to believe and obey God. Not dying means wanting to move God according to one’s own center.

This ideology must manifest on earth. For humans to truly qualify to bear a holy judgment, they must confront Satan with strength and stand in the correct position to win. To establish a perfect being who can make such a judgment, one must surpass the standard of a slightly imperfect being to become a perfect being. In other words, the position of trial and the value of existence must correspond to that content. One must confront what is real and push back against it.

The historical meaning of judgment is to have the strength to not be defeated by the history of evil and to remain until the end to organize it. Leaders of the democratic or communist world must not collapse in trials that they cannot handle; otherwise, it is not true. 

There is a method to forge Japan's famous sword. One must concentrate the spirit in one place, infuse it with the spirit of heaven and earth, and strike with a hammer. When one combines their own strength with the power of heaven and strikes with one hammer, our arteries will pulse. Knowing that we cannot avoid standing in the position of absolute judgment, how can we ensure the survival of the Unification Church?
We must consider whether we can create a church that can endure, even as the times pass and the ideologies of the world fade away. The question is whether the ideology of the Unification Church can remain. This is where the problem lies.

Are we prepared for this? What was the resolve of Jesus at the end, and what was He trying to convey? He desired the final judgment. An imperfect being cannot be accepted. Therefore, the teachings of Jesus do not end midway. Why has Christianity lost its power in the present age?

**Heart Judgment**

To this day, Christianity may not have established a standard of victory in the history of setting conditions for death or indemnity globally. However, God's desire is not merely the world of indemnity. It is the construction of the ideal world. As we approach this ideal world, the ultimate limit of the world of indemnity will appear. When we surpass that limit, we cannot remain in the same state of faith as in the past. What is needed here is the final world that humanity in the present age admires. It is the ideal world of God's original creation. A complete desire that encompasses and embraces everything... Being complete does not mean leaving one thing to do another. History moves toward that completeness.

The religion that has become the source of history and culture, reconciling itself at the final stage, proves that the final history is near. What should we, who stand at that last path, feel? Until now, God's providence has established conditions for indemnity from individuals to the world to eliminate sin. In other words, it has been a history of sacrifice. However, history does not begin with sacrifice and end with sacrifice. It is to abandon the history that began with sacrifice, to judge it, and to enter a new ideal world. From this standpoint, God desires perfect individuals, perfect families, and a perfect world that have passed through judgment and reached the ideal stage. Jesus could not teach that perfect ideal. It is not found in the Bible, no matter how one reads it.

Until now, religion has been separate from society. A religion that has the power to repel evil in the midst of the world of Satan must not be apart from life. That is the thorough standard of ideal living, being with God and on God's side. If God is on the inside, then humanity is on the outside, and it is one. If I rejoice, God rejoices too, and if God is sad, I am sad too. The value of a religion that has completed the purpose of that kind of religion is to understand its meaning and value, and we must fight through this end time with the view that the concept of religion is the source of our lives.

So what must our Unification Church do? We must not avoid judgment. Before God makes the final judgment on the world, we must judge ourselves. Based on what? Based on the center. What is the center? It is God. We must not judge based on God's external aspects or command relationships regarding the earth. We must judge with God's heart at the center. The issue is not simple. Therefore, what will move the future world is something that connects to God emotionally. Where there is that heart, there can be no peace.

So what is the heart? It encompasses everything that follows the nerves. It has the content and power to encompass all living concepts. Since the heart is in the position of the source of life, even if one denies life, one cannot deny the heart. Even if one denies existence, one cannot deny the heart. The heart exists prior to existence. Thus, God becomes love.

Now, let us assume that the Unification Church lives centered on the heart. Then what is the heart? We have never seen the heart. If we ask whether the heart is long, round, or high, we cannot answer. However, when we are with someone we love, it may seem like nothing, but when that person leaves, sorrow fills us. It fills us to the highest sensitivity of the nerves. The more we love, the more we can feel warmth.

We do not need a heart that can be measured by our five senses. It cannot be explained, but it is certainly overflowing. When we touch it, closed mouths open. Eyes that were crying shine and smile. A person who was lifeless becomes peaceful. If that disappears, it is miserable. If it is found, one can say the world is unnecessary.

If human hearts are like this, how much more will it be for those who have a relationship with God, the subject of absolute heart? This may not appear on the surface, but it undoubtedly exists. The Unification warriors are those who center on such a heart ideology and move toward a new world.

That nation is the ideal nation. It is not the current nation. It is formed by individuals who have surpassed the limits of heart judgment, gathering to create families, nations, and states.

The idea of "kill those who oppose" does not apply. If we leave those side effects as they are, nothing will remain. None will be forgiven. Therefore, do not kill the opponent; rather, elevate them. If I enter a position of dying, I can receive God's sympathy. Being in a truly happy position allows those in truly unhappy positions to live. Therefore, since crossing paths causes side effects, we should not cross but rather follow behind. This is God's love.

**Eternal Center**
